<div id="review_1610939821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610939821" />
    <a title="Glenn Sumi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28854579-glenn-sumi"><img alt="Glenn Sumi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444333567p2/28854579.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1610939821?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glenn Sumi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glenn Sumi" href="/user/show/28854579-glenn-sumi">Glenn Sumi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28854579-glenn-sumi?shelf=not-usa-can-uk">not-usa-can-uk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1610939821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8462467589625202648">This is my first Jo Nesbø novel, but it won’t be my last.<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461549038i/18879511.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I’ve wanted to read Nesbø for years, and the fact that this book – considered one of his best – is currently being made into a film, starring Michael Fassbender as the jaded, alcoholic Oslo detective Harry Hole, was a selling point. <br/><br/>I bought a three-eBook bundle for $4.99 (including Harry Hole books 7-9), and am so glad I went that route. It helped immensely to be able to search people and place names in seconds. Not being Norwegian, the </span>
  <span id="freeText8462467589625202648" style="display:none">This is my first Jo Nesbø novel, but it won’t be my last.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461549038i/18879511.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’ve wanted to read Nesbø for years, and the fact that this book – considered one of his best – is currently being made into a film, starring Michael Fassbender as the jaded, alcoholic Oslo detective Harry Hole, was a selling point. <br><br>I bought a three-eBook bundle for $4.99 (including Harry Hole books 7-9), and am so glad I went that route. It helped immensely to be able to search people and place names in seconds. Not being Norwegian, the names seemed daunting, so it was handy to able to press a button and see… “Aha! That’s where we met that person before!”<br> <br>In fact, I almost gave up in frustration. It took 75-100 pages to get oriented, long for a genre book. Nesbø gives us so many characters and a complicated time scheme – now it’s 1980, now 2004, now 1992, now 2004 again… What? How to follow?<br><br>I looked up some Goodreads reviews, and some people advised me to stick with it. I’m glad I did. Soon the plot, about the search for a serial killer who leaves snowmen outside his victims’ homes, began to go in a fascinating direction, the number of suspects (and victims) began adding up, and I was playing whodunit along with Harry and his intense new colleague, Katrina Bratt. <br><br>Among the characters in the book are a sleazy media type, a plastic surgeon with some secrets, and a disgraced cop looking to make a comeback. The book’s themes include colonialism in Africa, prostitution, rare diseases and paternity tests.<br><br>There’s a whiff of misogyny to the book that is disturbing, but I don’t know if that’s part of the culture or part of this specific book.<br><br>One scene set at a taping of one of Norway’s much-watched TV talk shows was so exciting it got me shouting “Yes” once I figured out what was going on. And the murder sequences can be quite gruesome. There’s one particular prop I’m eager to see on screen (although I might be shielding my eyes while watching); I just can’t picture how it works.<br><br>I didn’t find much depth to Hole, but I chalk that up to the fact that I’ve missed the previous six books. After reading the next two in the series, I may backtrack to fill in the gaps. <br><br>But in the meantime, I’m glad spring is here and there’s no more snow on the ground. After you read this book, you’ll know what I mean.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8462467589625202648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_240139571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240139571" />
    <a title="Morticia Adams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2623624-morticia-adams"><img alt="Morticia Adams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254079524p2/2623624.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240139571?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morticia Adams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morticia Adams" href="/user/show/2623624-morticia-adams">Morticia Adams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240139571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11390955795105191010">This might have been worth three stars, because I quite enjoyed it, but I’ve been stingy and given it just two, because of the disproportionate number of five star ratings it has, which I don’t think it deserves. It’s not a bad read by any means, the story is engaging, gripping at times, and genuinely creepy in places. But it’s far too long, so many red herrings it became tedious, and there were some utterly pointless non-sequiturs (eg the mould man, or was I missing some subtle reference there?</span>
  <span id="freeText11390955795105191010" style="display:none">This might have been worth three stars, because I quite enjoyed it, but I’ve been stingy and given it just two, because of the disproportionate number of five star ratings it has, which I don’t think it deserves. It’s not a bad read by any means, the story is engaging, gripping at times, and genuinely creepy in places. But it’s far too long, so many red herrings it became tedious, and there were some utterly pointless non-sequiturs (eg the mould man, or was I missing some subtle reference there?), and the writing is dreadfully clumsy (the sex scene in the first chapter had me helpless with laughter which I don’t think was the intention), and excessively detailed in description, as if the writer was thinking of the eventual film adaptation – and with some ruthless excisions, I’m sure this book would make a tense and entertaining two hour film, which is probably a better way to experience it than the much longer time it takes to read it. And I’ve read this week that Martin Scorsese, no less, has already signed up for it…. See: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/film/2011/nov/22/martin-scorsese-direct-thriller-snowman?newsfeed=true">http://www.guardian.co.uk/film/2011/n...</a><br /><br />I doubt very much whether I’ll read any more of Jo Nesbo’s novels, but I probably will go to see the film of the Snowman.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11390955795105191010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1133169953" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133169953" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133169953?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133169953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4804541506039848988">Nesbø creates his best novel in the series to date, placing Harry Hole and the larger cast of characters in a fast-paced race to discover Norway's first serial killer. Hole is investigating a number of murders in and around the Oslo area, after previous detectives could not find tangible clues to tie them together or offer any insight. Hole discovers that all the slain women are married mothers and that a snowman stands outside their residence, a beacon of sorts. Using the apt moniker "The Snowm</span>
  <span id="freeText4804541506039848988" style="display:none">Nesbø creates his best novel in the series to date, placing Harry Hole and the larger cast of characters in a fast-paced race to discover Norway's first serial killer. Hole is investigating a number of murders in and around the Oslo area, after previous detectives could not find tangible clues to tie them together or offer any insight. Hole discovers that all the slain women are married mothers and that a snowman stands outside their residence, a beacon of sorts. Using the apt moniker "The Snowman" for the killer, Hole works alongside a new partner, Katrine Bratt, and they expand the investigation, finding previous murders scattered throughout Norway. Further investigating sees Hole and Bratt discover a potential motive for the murders, children whose paternity is in question, unbeknownst to the fathers. As the case continues to heat up, Hole finds himself more drawn to Bratt on a number of levels, struggling with a past romance as well. The detectives work together and place a number of suspects in the crosshairs, only to discover that these are misdirections by the real killer. When Bratt is considered a prime suspect, Hole must fight with all he has to clear her name or detail her and stop the murdering rampage. Reconnecting with his ex, Rakel, Hole must also determine if she is safe from The Snowman, or if she could become another victim, as the killer seems focussed on personalising the act. A fabulous story that pushes Harry Hole to the brink on numerous occasions, Nesbø keeps readers begging for more.<br /><br />I have been anticipating getting to this novel in the series for a while. Having heard that it is the best of the collection, I can certainly see why, with Nesbø upping the ante from the start. The story is a compilation of many plots woven together and forces the reader not only to follow a complex murder investigation, but also subplots that do, eventually, play into the larger narrative. The introduction of Bratt as Hole's new partner harkens back to the plight of past detectives who worked alongside Hole. As the story pulls in so many directions, there is no doubt that the unfinished business left between Hole and Rakel must play some role, which substantiates the argument that she was highly important to Hole, even as many others are kept at arm's length. With his continued battles to wrestle with addiction, Hole becomes even more likeable in this story, as he pushes outside of his comfort zone to offer the reader more of a glimpse into his multi-faceted personality.<br /><br />Kudos Mr. Nesbø for another wonderful book. Can we expect even more pizzazz to come in the next novel?<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4804541506039848988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12348573427460906815"><br/>In this 7th book in the 'Harry Hole' series, Police Inspector Harry Hole investigates a number of disappearances and murders in Norway - which he suspects is the work of a serial killer. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555684844i/27385385.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Over about twenty years a number of women have disappeared, and one is known dead. In each case the woman is married and a mother. In a bizarre twist, a snowman has been left at the site of each disappearance, in one case wearing the pink scarf and containing the cell phone of the victim. This and an anonymous n</span>
  <span id="freeText12348573427460906815" style="display:none"><br>In this 7th book in the 'Harry Hole' series, Police Inspector Harry Hole investigates a number of disappearances and murders in Norway - which he suspects is the work of a serial killer. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555684844i/27385385.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Over about twenty years a number of women have disappeared, and one is known dead. In each case the woman is married and a mother. In a bizarre twist, a snowman has been left at the site of each disappearance, in one case wearing the pink scarf and containing the cell phone of the victim. This and an anonymous note sent to Harry lead to the killer being dubbed "The Snowman." <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555684844i/27385384.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Harry and his new partner Katrine Bratt, along with a small task force, are assigned to the case. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555684844i/27385383.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Harry and his team uncover a connection among the women a number of possible suspects come to light - one after another - each seeming to have a possible motive. Meanwhile, Harry struggles with his alcoholism while the love of his life, Rakel, prepares to move in with another man. On the lighter side Harry takes time to maintain his bond with Rakel's son Oleg and deals with a mold exterminator who dismantles his apartment. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555684844i/27385387.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>The characters in the story are well-developed, interesting, and often quirky and there are plenty of twists and turns. The book races along to a dramatic climax - where the murderer plans to stage a grande finale. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555684844i/27385386.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A compelling, well-written thriller, highly recommended.<br><br>You can follow my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot....</a></span>

  <span id="freeText18020332183717358840" style="display:none">This book met all my requirements for a good thriller:<br /><br />1) It kept me on the edge of my seat for much of the time, AND the loads of suspects and false leads kept me guessing.<br /><br />2) There were interesting characters with not too much backstory on each.<br /><br />3) The suspenseful and bloody buildup led to a satisfying conclusion.<br /><br />Strange, that what chilled me most about the book was not the creepy serial killer, but the thought of someone working diligently in my yard, making a snowman that stares not out onto the road, but directly into my house. <div id="review_2217364912" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2217364912" />
    <a title="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench"><img alt="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580443293p2/12766897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2217364912?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" href="/user/show/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench">Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781784704759" href="/book/show/33797954-the-snowman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=source-amazon-audible">source-amazon-audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2217364912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17096322677606517892">I think I may have fallen into a Jo Nesbø hole.<br/><br/>With a protagonist named (non-ironically) Harry Hole.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529273102ra/25809141.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Unfortunately, I've had shitacular luck with romance reads lately so I picked this up not realizing it was book 7 of a series. Oops. And now I can't unring this bell.<br/><br/>There are a couple references made to past events but they were minor and didn't detract from how engrossing this case was. <br/><br/>The Snowman is a serial killer targeting women. Their hallmark is leaving a snowman near the crime scene. <b>Spoo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17096322677606517892" style="display:none">I think I may have fallen into a Jo Nesbø hole.<br><br>With a protagonist named (non-ironically) Harry Hole.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529273102ra/25809141.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately, I've had shitacular luck with romance reads lately so I picked this up not realizing it was book 7 of a series. Oops. And now I can't unring this bell.<br><br>There are a couple references made to past events but they were minor and didn't detract from how engrossing this case was. <br><br>The Snowman is a serial killer targeting women. Their hallmark is leaving a snowman near the crime scene. <b>Spooky. As. Fuck.</b><br><br>The case is full of twists and turns that felt authentic when trying to solve a serial killer case. Some may see them as red herrings but most of them are pretty obvious to the reader, so I never found them frustrating.<br><br>I really liked the way Nesbø constructed this narrative with Americana references, the way he folded in song lyrics and most especially Harry's characterization as a flawed individual who is well aware of his flaws but helpless to alter them. Both his relationship with Rakel and Oleg to a lesser extent I found moving. There are multiple POVs and one of those is the killer's and all of them had a distinct voice.<br><br>Needless to say, I'll be reading more from this series. I'm SUPER tempted to read the next one to figure out what the deal is with that random dangler but I want to know of Harry's beginnings. Decisions are hard.<br><br>Recommended to suspense thriller fans.</span>

<div id="review_349842642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349842642" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349842642?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349842642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8216433079514027623">This was a really good mystery/thriller. One of the best I've read in awhile. The author has you following Harry Hole around as he investigates a string of murders involving married women with children. You have been given easy clues, but there are still red herrings. Like any real investigation, we have to go through a process of elimination. But,after a few dead ends, the author practically hits you over the head with a brick, so if you were paying any attention, you know who "The Snowman" is.</span>
  <span id="freeText8216433079514027623" style="display:none">This was a really good mystery/thriller. One of the best I've read in awhile. The author has you following Harry Hole around as he investigates a string of murders involving married women with children. You have been given easy clues, but there are still red herrings. Like any real investigation, we have to go through a process of elimination. But,after a few dead ends, the author practically hits you over the head with a brick, so if you were paying any attention, you know who "The Snowman" is. But, then, a feeling of real dread starts to form. I felt like screaming at Harry. I saw what was happening and felt helpless to stop it. I couldn't put the book down. Very clever! <br />This was my first novel by Jo Nesbo, but it won't be my last. in fact, I'm am adding more of his books to my wish list. Over all an A.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2361655005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2361655005" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2361655005?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2361655005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12540145050339688582">Two parts mystery and one part thriller, this was all good Jo Nesbo writing.<br/><br/>Nesbo’s 2007 Harry Hole book, the seventh in the series, finds our alcoholic, tough guy detective finally finding himself on the trail of a Norwegian serial killer. This has been a running put-on up to now, since Hole went to Australia and ended that serial killer run. Nesbo alludes to some American FBI training Hole had before this book and when the clues start adding up to a Norse multi-murderer many in the department </span>
  <span id="freeText12540145050339688582" style="display:none">Two parts mystery and one part thriller, this was all good Jo Nesbo writing.<br><br>Nesbo’s 2007 Harry Hole book, the seventh in the series, finds our alcoholic, tough guy detective finally finding himself on the trail of a Norwegian serial killer. This has been a running put-on up to now, since Hole went to Australia and ended that serial killer run. Nesbo alludes to some American FBI training Hole had before this book and when the clues start adding up to a Norse multi-murderer many in the department accuse Harry of crying wolf.<br><br>But of course our hero knows a clue when he sees it and picks up the scent and off we go.<br><br>In the dark, cold and snowy setting of Nordic noir writing, Nesbo has us explore themes of family, separation, betrayal and revenge. There is a statistic mentioned in the book that as high as one in five children have a different father than who they believe ands that women, like some species of animal, are programmed to be attracted to mates outside of monogamy. When this infidelity results in moral and genetic problems, problems ensue, for the victims and for Harry who finds himself all tied up in finding the killer in time.<br><br>I enjoy Nesbo’s writing, but he can be inconsistent and sometimes hard to follow. Interjecting backstory sporadically throughout the story, we piece together the clues as does Hole to find the killer. Like his 2002 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3522419.Nemesis__Harry_Hole___4_" title="Nemesis (Harry Hole, #4) by Jo Nesbø" rel="nofollow noopener">Nemesis</a>, he can also throw in too many sub-plots and can get the story tangled up.<br><br>All in all, though, this is a good story and the ending more than made up for some slow back miles in the middle.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524055866i/25396552.jpg" width="400" height="292" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12540145050339688582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1667051985" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1667051985" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1667051985?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099520276" href="/book/show/7779827-the-snowman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1667051985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17913908474898055731">I had a little trouble getting into this book but once I did it was gripping and very creepy in places. However, I found it overly long and felt that the complex plot could have been simplified a tad to keep the tension high between killings. As usual for Jo Nesbo the writing was strong and the plot had sufficient false leads and red herrings to make it difficult to identify the killer (although there are early clues pointing in the right direction if you're watching carefully).<br/><br/>In the Snowman, H</span>
  <span id="freeText17913908474898055731" style="display:none">I had a little trouble getting into this book but once I did it was gripping and very creepy in places. However, I found it overly long and felt that the complex plot could have been simplified a tad to keep the tension high between killings. As usual for Jo Nesbo the writing was strong and the plot had sufficient false leads and red herrings to make it difficult to identify the killer (although there are early clues pointing in the right direction if you're watching carefully).<br /><br />In the Snowman, Harry Hole finally has a serial killer to track down in Norway, the first ever apparently. As usual, he is portrayed as a loner, struggling to stay away from alcohol and still in two minds about his ex-wife Rakel. Not liked by any of the hierarchy in the police force because of his independent streak, they would be happy to see him make a serious error and be dismissed, however Harry continues to disappoint them by being the one to make the breakthroughs. There were some very dark and creepy scenes in this book and a very high drama, action packed ending. Nesbo's descriptions of the cold and snowy landscape are very evocative and add to the chilliness of the crimes. I'm sure that every time I see a snowman in future I will think of this novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17913908474898055731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qtjuBIB7yQequ0Vmw4Gamip9lbz+a7UddGE5AgGbYs6Q/ofWOyUAbw2Q8Qc0dJBF/CJydDDmO3ovH3+zzNiQVA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bfvyAdjfUw6jBorvLdPbTLAoJXWlK7RntmO5bJ8hv9VX3ZvTY4GaZgQtPo7aJtGTZnfCvWumOgDtHf/dUmJNTw==')})
  }

The killer is still at large, and there’s <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16474819515524142048\" style=\"display:none\">Prepare for The Hypnotist to cast its spell\n\nIn the frigid clime of Tumba, Sweden, a gruesome triple homicide attracts the interest of Detective Inspector Joona Linna, who demands to investigate the murders. The killer is still at large, and there’s only one surviving witness—the boy whose family was killed before his eyes. Whoever committed the crimes wanted this boy to die: he’s suffered more than one hundred knife wounds and lapsed into a state of shock. He enlists Dr. Erik Maria Bark to mesmerize the boy, hoping to discover the killer through his eyes.\n\nIt’s the sort of work that Bark has sworn he would never do again—ethically dubious and psychically scarring. De gör det regelbundet trots att det inte finns något enda dokumenterat fall där ett medium bidragit till en lösning.\n\nFlora Hansen kallar sig för spiritistiskt medium och har <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16300151456038036156\" style=\"display:none\">I hela världen tar polisen hjälp av andliga medier vid svåra utredningar. De gör det regelbundet trots att det inte finns något enda dokumenterat fall där ett medium bidragit till en lösning.\n\nFlora Hansen kallar sig för spiritistiskt medium och har i många år försörjt sig på att låtsas att hon kan tala med de döda. En kväll i augusti läser hon på löpsedlarna om ett fruktansvärt mord som skett på en sluten anstalt för unga kvinnor med destruktivt beteende. Flora Hansen bestämmer sig för att ringa polisen och hävda att hon har kommit i kontakt med den dödas ande.\n\nDen tekniska undersökningen pekar entydigt på att mördaren är en av de intagna, en snäll och tystlåten flicka som rymde från anstalten samma natt som mordet skedde. När Joona Linna börjar undersöka hennes förflutna visar det sig att hon inte alltid varit så snäll.\n\nJoona har redan stannat längre på denna brottsplats än vad någon annan kommissarie skulle göra. Ändå är han inte färdig, han tänker att han måste se ytterligare någonting för att bli utsläppt från detta fruktansvärda rum, han måste hitta en detalj som kan leda vidare, som kan föra tråden som en nål.\nHan ser på flickan i sängen. En svag värme utstrålar fortfarande från den nakna huden. Hennes händer ligger över ansiktet, som om hon lekte kurragömma. Han lutar sig försiktigt över henne och upptäcker att någonting har fastnat under hennes vänstra pekfingernagel. Det ser ut som ett djuprött sandkorn, en flisa av en rubin.\nHan blinkar och försöker skärpa blicken. Det är svårt att koncentrera sig på detta lilla röda korn i ett rum nerstänkt av blod, men han ger sig inte, han lutar sig bara närmare, känner den söta doften från henne och förstår plötsligt vad det är han ser under nageln.\n\nJakten på förövaren tar gång på gång våldsamma och oväntade vändingar. Varje svar tycks bara leda till nya gåtor, och det som nyss var enkelt är plötsligt labyrintiskt.\nMen trots att utredningen hamnar i en återvändsgränd ignorerar polisen Flora Hansens telefonsamtal. Först begär hon pengar för sina upplysningar, men sedan ber hon dem bara att lyssna, allt mer desperat.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16300151456038036156\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15949702439841225651">Jo Nesbø is a bestselling Norwegian author and musician. He was born in Oslo and grew up in Molde. Nesbø graduated from the Norwegian School of Economics with a degree in economics. Nesbø is primarily famous for his crime novels about Detective Harry Hole, but he is also the main vocals and songwriter for the Norwegian rock band Di Derre. In 2007 Nesbø also released his first children's book, Dokt</span>
  <span id="freeText15949702439841225651" style="display:none">Jo Nesbø is a bestselling Norwegian author and musician. He was born in Oslo and grew up in Molde. Nesbø graduated from the Norwegian School of Economics with a degree in economics. Nesbø is primarily famous for his crime novels about Detective Harry Hole, but he is also the main vocals and songwriter for the Norwegian rock band Di Derre. In 2007 Nesbø also released his first children's book, Doktor Proktors Prompepulver.<br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51155-harry-hole" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Hole</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/66741-doktor-proktor" rel="nofollow noopener">Doktor Proktor</a><br /><br />For exclusive content about Jo Nesbø and his books, register for the official fan newsletter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://jonesbo.com/newsletter/">https://jonesbo.com/newsletter/</a></span>

A brilliant and epic novel, breathtaking in its scope and design—winner of The Glass Key for best Nordic crime novel and selected<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7834499485359213706\" style=\"display:none\">The Redbreast is a fabulous introduction to Nesbø’s tough-as-nails series protagonist, Oslo police detective Harry Hole.
